# Fault Localization: NFS Mount Disappears Due to Inode Revalidate Failure

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 4.1.15
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: File System
- **Component**: NFS / SunRPC

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 117651
**Summary**: Root NFS and autofs - mount disappears due to inode revalidate failed
**Regression**: Yes (works on 3.14.12, broken on 4.1.15)

After upgrading from 3.14.12 to 4.1.15 I've got strange behaviour with autofs.

It happens on diskless machine with root on NFS. There is autofs indirect mount on /storage, where NFS volumes are mounted on demand.

Everything mounts normally, but after mount expiration (during unmount) autofs mount disappears - that is, not only /storage/<volume> unmounts, but /storage is also unmounted. This happens quite often - usually on the very first expiration.

automount logs umount error in such cases.

Without autofs, mount/umount of the same NFS volume works correctly.

With NFS debug enabled, I've got following errors:

```
NFS reply getattr: -512
nfs_revalidate_inode: (0:15/6291480) getattr failed, error=-512
NFS: nfs_lookup_revalidate(/storage) is invalid
```

After inode revalidate failure all mounts on this inode are unmounted and so autofs mount disappears, while automount daemon itself continue to run.

tcpdump shows, that server replies to getattr without error, but client doesn't see this reply, and returning error instead.

I am ready to supply additional information.

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files
3. Narrow down to the specific file(s) and function(s)/data structure(s) that contain the bug or need modification
4. Write your findings to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` in the following format:

```json
{
  "buggy_files": ["path/to/file.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["function_or_struct_name"],
  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

## Success Criteria

- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy file(s)
- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy function(s) or data structure(s)
- [ ] Write results to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`
- [ ] Provide reasoning for the localization

     9→  "reasoning": "The bug occurs when an RPC call (NFS getattr) receives a signal during the wait phase. The rpc_wait_bit_killable callback checks for pending signals WITHOUT verifying if the RPC_TASK_QUEUED bit has actually been cleared by a completed response. When a signal arrives, rpc_wait_bit_killable returns -ERESTARTSYS even if the RPC response has been received and the bit has been cleared. This causes the RPC call to exit with error -512 (ERESTARTSYS) despite the server successfully sending a response. The NFS client then treats this as a permanent failure, causing inode revalidation to fail and leading to mount invalidation. The fix requires modifying rpc_wait_bit_killable to check if the wait bit is still set before returning -ERESTARTSYS; if the bit has been cleared, the response has arrived and should be processed with return value 0 instead of -ERESTARTSYS. This impacts the nfs_lookup_revalidate and __nfs_revalidate_inode functions which depend on rpc_call_sync for getattr operations."
    10→}

133-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the fault localization analysis. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Fault Localization Summary

**Buggy File**: `net/sunrpc/sched.c`
**Buggy Function**: `rpc_wait_bit_killable`
**Confidence**: 0.85

### Root Cause Analysis

The NFS mount disappearance bug is caused by improper signal handling in the RPC layer:

1. **The Problem**: The `rpc_wait_bit_killable` callback function (line 253-259) checks for pending signals **without verifying if the RPC_TASK_QUEUED bit has actually been cleared** by an arriving response.

2. **The Scenario**:
   - An RPC call (NFS getattr) waits for a response with TASK_KILLABLE mode
   - The server sends a valid response, setting `rq_reply_bytes_recvd` and clearing the RPC_TASK_QUEUED bit
   - A signal arrives at this critical moment
   - `rpc_wait_bit_killable` checks `fatal_signal_pending()` and returns -ERESTARTSYS
   - The RPC call exits with error -512 despite the response being received

3. **The Impact**:
   - The error propagates to `__nfs_revalidate_inode()` which treats it as a permanent failure
   - This causes `nfs_lookup_verify_inode()` to return non-zero (error)
   - `nfs_lookup_revalidate()` interprets this as invalid and invalidates the lookup
   - The dentry cache is invalidated and the mount disappears

4. **The Fix**: Check if the wait bit has been cleared before returning -ERESTARTSYS. If the bit is cleared, the response has already arrived and should be processed normally instead of being treated as a signal-interrupted error.

The results have been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`.

  "content": "{\n  \"buggy_files\": [\n    \"net/sunrpc/sched.c\"\n  ],\n  \"buggy_functions\": [\n    \"rpc_wait_bit_killable\"\n  ],\n  \"confidence\": 0.85,\n  \"reasoning\": \"The bug occurs when an RPC call (NFS getattr) receives a signal during the wait phase. The rpc_wait_bit_killable callback checks for pending signals WITHOUT verifying if the RPC_TASK_QUEUED bit has actually been cleared by a completed response. When a signal arrives, rpc_wait_bit_killable returns -ERESTARTSYS even if the RPC response has been received and the bit has been cleared. This causes the RPC call to exit with error -512 (ERESTARTSYS) despite the server successfully sending a response. The NFS client then treats this as a permanent failure, causing inode revalidation to fail and leading to mount invalidation. The fix requires modifying rpc_wait_bit_killable to check if the wait bit is still set before returning -ERESTARTSYS; if the bit has been cleared, the response has arrived and should be processed with return value 0 instead of -ERESTARTSYS. This impacts the nfs_lookup_revalidate and __nfs_revalidate_inode functions which depend on rpc_call_sync for getattr operations.\"\n}\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/fault_localization_result.json"

When a signal arrives, rpc_wait_bit_killable returns -ERESTARTSYS even if the RPC response has been received and the bit has been cleared. The rpc_wait_bit_killable callback checks for pending signals WITHOUT verifying if the RPC_TASK_QUEUED bit has actually been cleared by a completed response. When a signal arrives, rpc_wait_bit_killable returns -ERESTARTSYS even if the RPC response has been received and the bit has been cleared. This causes the RPC call to exit with error -512 (ERESTARTSYS) despite the server successfully sending a response. The NFS client then treats this as a permanent failure, causing inode revalidation to fail and leading to mount invalidation. The fix requires modifying rpc_wait_bit_killable to check if the wait bit is still set before returning -ERESTARTSYS; if the bit has been cleared, the response has arrived and should be processed with return value 0 instead of -ERESTARTSYS. This impacts the nfs_lookup_revalidate and __nfs_revalidate_inode functions which depend on rpc_call_sync for getattr operations.\"\n}\n",
    "filePath": "/workspace/fault_localization_result.json",
    "numLines": 11,
    "startLine": 1,
    "totalLines": 11
  },
  "type": "text"
}

      

      

        Code Changes (1)
        
1. WRITE /workspace/fault_localization_result.json
{
  "buggy_files": [
    "net/sunrpc/sched.c"
  ],
  "buggy_functions": [
    "rpc_wait_bit_killable"
  ],
  "confidence": 0.85,
  "reasoning": "The bug occurs when an RPC call (NFS getattr) receives a signal during the wait phase. The rpc_wait_bit_killable callback checks for pending signals WITHOUT verifying if the RPC_TASK_QUEUED bit has actually been cleared by a completed response. When a signal arrives, rpc_wait_bit_killable returns -ERESTARTSYS even if the RPC response has been received and the bit has been cleared. This causes the RPC call to exit with error -512 (ERESTARTSYS) despite the server successfully sending a response. The NFS client then treats this as a permanent failure, causing inode revalidation to fail and leading to mount invalidation. The fix requires modifying rpc_wait_bit_killable to check if the wait bit is still set before returning -ERESTARTSYS; if the bit has been cleared, the response has arrived and should be processed with return value 0 instead of -ERESTARTSYS. This impacts the nfs_lookup_revalidate and __nfs_revalidate_inode functions which depend on rpc_call_sync for getattr operations."
}
